## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the population growth rate (dP/dt) as a function of time (t) and current population (P). This is a classic population dynamics problem where the growth rate depends on the population size, potentially exhibiting density-dependent effects like logistic growth, Allee effects, or other ecological feedback mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P (Malthusian/exponential growth, density-independent)
- Logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 * P) (Gompertz model for bounded growth)
- Theta-logistic growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P**c2) (generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (1 + c2 * P) (growth with strong Allee effect and carrying capacity)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 * (1 + c2 * P) (power-law growth with density limitation)
- Richards growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + (c1 * P)**c2) (Richards/generalized logistic model)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with hyperbolic saturation)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (polynomial density dependence)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects, e.g., Allee + carrying capacity)
- Time-dependent exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth rate changing exponentially with time)
- von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 + c2 * P (anabolic-catabolic balance model)
- Hassell-type growth: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P)**c2 (generalized density-dependent regulation)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear proportionality to P → Exponential/Malthusian growth: dP_dt = c*P indicates density-independent reproduction
- Quadratic P term (P²) with opposite sign to linear P → Logistic-type density-dependent regulation with carrying capacity
- Product of two linear factors in P → Allee effect or bistability: growth rate zero at two population thresholds
- Logarithmic dependence on P → Gompertz-type growth where per-capita rate declines logarithmically with population
- Ratio P/(1+cP) → Saturating per-capita resource acquisition (contest competition)
- Fractional power P^c with c<1 → Sub-linear growth from resource limitation or metabolic scaling
- Explicit time dependence in growth rate → Non-autonomous dynamics from environmental forcing or seasonal variation
- Growth rate approaching zero at large P → Carrying capacity; mathematically requires negative higher-order P terms or saturating forms
